142311339X|5.0|The long awaited sequel to the Percy Jackson and the Olympian series, The Lost Hero, does not disappoint the rabid fanatics of the previous series, me being one of them. It is book one of the new series by Rick Riordan: Heroes of Olympus, and it may be one of Rick Riordan's best work. It seemed to cast a spell on me from the very beginning until the end. The book brings the readers back into the world of Greek mythology, and still includes some of the characters from the previous Percy Jackson and the Olympians series. It also introduces some very well developed new characters. In the world created by Rick Riordan, Greek gods and goddesses are very real. They rule the world from Mount Olympus and each god controls a various aspect of the world. For example, Zeus, king of the gods, controls the skies and lightning and Poseidon controls the seas. However, occasionally these gods and goddesses fall in love with a mortal and have children with them. These are the protagonists of Heroes of Olympus. They are called demigods which means half mortal and half god. In the previous series the main protagonist is Percy Jackson, who is the son of Poseidon: God of the Seas. In The Lost Hero, Percy is discovered missing for three days and his girlfriend, Annabeth is frantically searching for him.     The story begins by introducing three new characters: Jason, Piper, and Leo. They all go to a boarding school for \\"unstable\\" children called The Wilderness School.  Jason is a very muscular and handsome boy and is the main demigod in The Lost Hero. Piper is a girl who is extremely breathtaking, even without make up. She is shy, but as later shown in the book by her actions, very courageous. She has a crush on Jason and at the beginning of the book they are a couple. Leo is Jason's best friend who has a very strong sense of humor, but can also be a bit annoying sometimes.   At the beginning of the book Jason Piper, and Leo are on the bus to a field trip to the Grand Canyon. Jason has no idea how he got there and cannot remember anything of his past. Piper and Leo are very puzzled by this and think he is joking at first. Then they realize that he is serious and are flabbergasted. At the end of the field trip, they are attacked by a group of storm spirits which are a part of Greek mythology. Their chaperone and gym teacher, Coach Hedge, turns out to be a satyr. This is the Greek term for a creature that is half man, half goat. Jason, Piper, and Leo are dazed and shocked by this, but have to deal with the threat at hand. In the end, Coach Hedge sacrifices himself so that Jason, Piper, and Leo can escape. Moments after the storm spirits and Coach Hedge disappear, a girl with blonde hair and storm gray eyes appears above them flying on a chariot. She introduces herself to them as Annabeth, a character from the previous Percy Jackson and the Olympians series. She is the daughter of Athena, the goddess of wisdom. She explains to them what their true identities are: Demigods. She also explains that in order for them to be safe from monsters such as the storm spirits, she has to take them to a special camp for Demigods like them. It is called Camp Half-Blood. This is where Demigods train to fight monsters like storm spirits and are sent on heroic quests to save the world. After nearly facing death, the three of them gladly allow themselves to be whisked off to the safety of Camp Half-Blood. Once there, they find hundreds of Demigods all with different godly parents. They each have unique powers depending on their parent. For example, the sons of Zeus have the power to control the air around them and summon lightning. It is later revealed that Jason is a son of Zeus, Piper a daughter of Aphrodite, and Leo is a son of Hephaestus. Aphrodite is the goddess of love and beauty and Hephaestus is the god of the forge and engineering. After they settle in at Camp Half-Blood, they discover that Hera, goddess of marriage, has been kidnapped. Jason, Piper, and Leo are then sent on a quest to rescue her. However, Piper has a secret that she cannot reveal to the other two which causes an extremely interesting plot twist at the end and completely changes the course of their quest. At the end of the quest, Jason finally discovers his true identity and how he came to Piper and Leo. He also has a very good guess as to where Percy Jackson has disappeared to.    It is a complex book in terms of the plot and is truly unpredictable. It is chalk full of lies, betrayals, courageous acts, and many plot twists. By the end of the book, Riordan introduces a whole new side to the world of Greek mythology that he created. It leaves us with endless possibilities.    I can honestly say that it is the best book I have read all year and am counting down the days until the sequel comes out. The book surprisingly made me laugh at many points out loud, which books do not often do. At the same time, there were points where my heart started thumping against my chest because of the suspense. It is a wild roller-coaster ride that was very refreshing after reading many disappointing and boring fiction books.    Another great thing about this book is that even though these Demigods are off on a quest that determines the fate of the world, there are still moments where I am reminded that they are also normal teenagers. I found that I could relate to some of their conflicts in the book. For example, when Piper started feeling guilty about keeping her secret from her two friends, I was reminded of many times when I kept secrets from my friends and the guilt I felt from not telling them. Riordan captures emotions very well, without the use of complex words. This is one of my favorite things about the book.    Another great thing about the book is just how interesting the world of Greek mythology Riordan creates is. It is simply genius. He creates a world where a civilization as old as the Greeks is incorporated with the twenty-first century. I think teenagers around my age would greatly enjoy this book as almost all the characters of the book are our age. They are incredibly complex at times, yet Riordan conveys their feelings with ease. It is very comparable to the Harry Potter series. In both series, teenagers are suddenly whisked off to learn their true magical identities and begin a new life in a place such as Hogwarts or Camp Half-Blood.   Overall, I strongly recommend this book to anyone who enjoys fantasy and kids around my age. It is an action packed book that is extremely unpredictable and, for the most part, is an easy read. In other words, it is just the kind of book kids my age would enjoy the most. I think it rightfully earns a place next to Harry Potter and many others as one of the greatest children fantasy books.

1439107955|5.0|Nearly two years ago, at age 20, I was diagnosed with leukemia.  I relocated back home from college and immediately began nine months of intensive chemotherapy.  I was quickly in remission and have been on maintenance therapy for over a year now.    I have never been someone very interested in the scientific world. It is very unlikely that prior to being diagnosed with cancer that I would have ever glanced at this book, let alone have read it.    But, \\"leukemia is like that... it changes your life.\\"    I didn't have much interest in learning about the disease at first.  All I wanted from my doctors was the bottom line: how I rid myself of the cancer, how I avoid the side effects, how I escape the confines of the pediatric oncology floor.    One of the cancer social networks that I follow originally posted an NPR story about this book.  Then I saw the New York Times piece.  I finally typed in the title to Amazon and read the introduction, which was available for free. The way the author spoke about Carla, who happened to have the same diagnosis as me, instantly grabbed my attention.    Whether or not it was just a matter of time before I was ready to intellectually confront the disease which has consumed much of my life for the past two years, I'm not sure. I had already confronted it physically and emotionally.  Perhaps it was just a random set of events that led me to purchase this book.  Regardless, once I received it, I couldn't set it down.  I was acutely and passionately enthralled with learning: taking notes of poignant quotes I identified with, writing down questions for my doctors, and reading aloud parts to my family that I thought they would find interesting.    I was very impressed by the text.  Not only for the compelling way the author writes about everything from his relationship with patients to complex genetic theories, but for encapsulating so much of what I was curious about, as a patient, in a single book.  For me, it answered so much of what I wanted to know... not only about the causes, the history, the biology, and the chemistry of cancer - which it did - but about the fears and hopes concerning my own diagnosis and the future of cancer treatment.    I can only imagine how much time, blood, sweat, and tears went into creating The Emperor of All Maladies.  What I do know is that it had a deep and positive influence on my life.

0812973992|5.0|Let The Great World Spin was a book club selection, which was enjoyed by all who attended, and it prompted a lively, intelligent discussion. The story is based on the lives of eleven characters on the day in 1974 when French funambulist, Philippe Petit, danced across a wire (tightrope) secured between the new twin towers at the World Trade Center in New York. It is a well-written, literary masterpiece with highly believable, three-dimensional (complicated) characters.<br /><br />The characters are extremely diverse, and include an Irish immigrant \\"monk\\" with a heart of gold, a Park Avenue wife of a judge/mother of a son who was killed in Vietnam, a Guatemalan nurse to a young artist trying to kick a cocaine habit and living a 1920s lifestyle, a heroin-addicted streetwalking prostitute and her daughter and two young children. There is also a chapter where seemingly unrelated characters in Palo Alto, CA--a group of pioneering computer hackers--find a way to contact payphones in Manhattan on the day of Petit's performance, and try to get a live blow-by-blow account of the event from eye-witnesses. It's a reminder to the reader of the state of technology at the time, and how different the world of 1974 was from today, when the event, no doubt, would have been broadcast on every television station and the Internet.<br /><br />This prompted our group to discuss our own \\"day-in-the-life\\" experiences we had on Sept. 11, when we first heard of the attacks on the twin towers. Not surprisingly, everyone in the room watched the horrendous events unfold on television.<br /><br />The high wire event loosely connects all the characters and it feels as though the lives are spinning and folding atop one another in unexpected ways. In spite of the darkness and at times, overwhelming grief associated with these character's lives, the reader is left satisfied and reminded how different (and important) each life and each character's personal story is.<br /><br />I give this book my highest recommendation.<br /><br />Michele Cozzens is the author of [[ASIN:193217236X Irish Twins]].ozzens is the author of [[ASIN:193217236X Irish Twins]].

B004BSIJ9Q|4.0|Kanye West is nowhere near is as talented, innovative, or original as he and his adherents believe, and the themes he explores on this album (decadence, excess, existential despair and individual moral degradation) have been explored countless times in all forms of art for centuries.<br /><br />But I cannot help but admit that I find this the most ambitious, interesting, and coherent album a hip hop or pop artist has produced in ages. One of the chief criticisms that anti-hip-hop critics and fans commonly make, is that its not \\"music\\". This is music, with a diverse and eerie set of samples painstakingly woven into something that approaches an apocalyptic symphony, one not so easy to turn away from.
